Thought:
Let's find the HCF of (2272-N) and (875-N) to get the value of N.
2272 - N = (2^4) * (11) * (N1) and 875 - N = (5^3) * (N2)
Since the remainder is the same, we can say that N1 = N2 = K (some constant)
Therefore, (2^4) * (11) * K - N = (5^3) * K - N
Simplifying, we get N = 125K - 44K = 81K
The sum of the digits of N = 8 + 1 + K
We need to find the value of K.
N is a 3-digit number, so K can be 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, or 9.
Let's try each value of K and see which one gives us a 3-digit number.
For K = 1, N = 81, which is a 2-digit number.
For K = 2, N = 162, which is a 3-digit number.
Therefore, the sum of the digits of N is 1 + 6 + 2 = 9.

Therefore, N = 1397.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 69 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: By himself, Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours. On a particular day, he happens to finish two-thirds of the work. The remaining portion of the work is done by Jill, whose rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do. How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 8
  C: 22
  D: 50
  E: 20
Response 0:
Thought:
  Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours, so his rate of cleaning is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.
  On a particular day, Jack finishes two-thirds of the work, so the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill.
  Let's assume that the yacht is one unit of work.
  Jack finishes two-thirds of the work, which is (2/3) * 1 = 2/3 of the yacht.
  The remaining one-third of the yacht is (1/3) * 1 = 1/3 of the yacht.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of Jack's rate of cleaning, so her rate of cleaning is (5/100) * (1/12) = 1/240 of the yacht per hour.
  Let's assume that Jill takes x hours to finish the remaining work.
  Therefore, Jill can clean (1/240) * x of the yacht in x hours.
  Jack has already cleaned 2/3 of the yacht, so the remaining 1/3 of the yacht is cleaned by Jill.
  Therefore, (1/240) * x = (1/3) - (2/3) = 1/3 - 2/3 = -1/3
  Solving for x, we get x = (-1/3) / (1/240) = 80
  Therefore, it takes Jill 80 hours to finish the remaining work.
  The answer is E: 20.
Action: Answer("E")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours.
  Jack completes 2/3 of the work.
  Therefore, the remaining 1/3 of the work is done by Jill.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of what Jack can do.
  Let's assume that Jill takes x hours to complete the remaining 1/3 of the work.
  Jack's rate of cleaning is 1/12 of the yacht per hour.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is 5/100 * 1/12 = 1/240 of the yacht per hour.
  Using the formula: rate * time = work, we can set up the equation:
  (1/12) * (2/3) + (1/240) * x = (1/3)
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 8
  Therefore, it takes Jill 8 hours to finish the remaining work.
  The answer is B: 8.

  Using the work formula, we can set up the equation:
  Work done by Jack + Work done by Jill = 1 (the whole work)
  Two-thirds of the work done by Jack + One-third of the work done by Jill = 1
  (2/3) * (1/12) * t + (1/3) * (1/20) * x = 1
  where t is the time Jack took to finish two-thirds of the work.
  We know that t = (2/3) * 12 = 8 hours.
  Substituting t = 8, we get:
  (2/3) * (1/12) * 8 + (1/3) * (1/20) * x = 1
  Solving for x, we get:
  x = 22.5 hours
  Since we are looking for a whole number of hours, the answer is 22.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 22.

  Therefore, Jill can do 1/20 * t units of work in t hours.
  Jack has already done 24 units of work.
  Therefore, the remaining 12 units of work will take (12 / (1/12)) = 144 hours if Jack does it alone.
  Jack and Jill together can do the remaining work in t hours.
  Therefore, Jack can do (1/12 * t) units of work in t hours.
  Jill can do (1/20 * t) units of work in t hours.
  Together, they can do (1/12 * t) + (1/20 * t) units of work in t hours.
  (1/12 * t) + (1/20 * t) = 12
  Solving the above equation, we get t = 22.5 hours.
  Therefore, it will take Jill 22.5 hours to finish the remaining work.

  Jack can clean a yacht in 12 hours.
  Therefore, Jack's rate of cleaning is 1 yacht/12 hours = 1/12 yacht/hour.
  On a particular day, Jack finished two-thirds of the work.
  Therefore, the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill to do.
  Jill's rate of cleaning is just 5% of what Jack can do.
  Therefore, Jill's rate of cleaning is 5/100 * (1/12) yacht/hour = 1/240 yacht/hour.
  Let's assume it takes Jill "x" hours to finish the remaining work.
  Therefore, Jill can do 1/x of the work in an hour.
  We know that Jack finished two-thirds of the work.
  Therefore, the remaining one-third of the work is left for Jill to do.
  Therefore, (1/3) of the work is done by Jill in "x" hours.
  We can equate the two rates of work to find "x".
  (1/3) = (1/240) * x
  x = (1/3) * 240
  x = 80
  Therefore, it takes Jill 80 hours to finish the remaining work.
  The answer is E: 20.

Question: Mr.Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. He loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train. How long would he have taken if he had traveled by car in both ways?
Choices:
  A: 22 hrs
  B: 18 hrs
  C: 16 hrs
  D: 20 hrs
  E: 13 hrs
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel to the city by train is 'x' hours.
  Therefore, the time taken by Mr. Sam to return by car is also 'x' hours.
  According to the problem, Mr. Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to the city and return by car.
  Therefore, the total time taken by Mr. Sam = time taken to go by train + time taken to return by car
  Total time taken = x + x = 2x
  But, he loses 4 hours if he goes both ways by train.
  Therefore, the total time taken by Mr. Sam if he goes both ways by train = 17 + 17 - 4 = 30 hours
  The time taken by Mr. Sam to travel by car in both ways = Total time taken - time taken to go by train - time taken to return by car
  Time taken by Mr. Sam to travel by car in both ways = 30 - x - x = 30 - 2x
  We need to find the value of 'x' to calculate the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel by car in both ways.
  Let's solve the equation 2x + 4 = 30
  2x = 26
  x = 13
  Therefore, the time taken by Mr. Sam to travel by car in both ways = 30 - 2x = 30 - 2(13) = 4 hours.
  The answer is E: 13 hrs.
Action: Answer("E")

Topic: Math
Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought?
Choices:
  A: 4
  B: 3
  C: 2
  D: 1
  E: 0
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the coin-diver brought x copper coins and y brass coins.
  From the problem, we know that the coin-diver gets 20 cents for each copper coin and 25 cents for each brass coin.
  Therefore, the total amount of money the coin-diver gets is 20x + 25y cents.
  We also know that the total amount of money the coin-diver got after one dive is $3.40 or 340 cents.
  So, we can write the following equation: 20x + 25y = 340.
  We need to find the minimum number of copper coins that the coin-diver brought, which means we need to minimize the value of x.
  Let's try to solve for x in terms of y.
  20x + 25y = 340
  20x = 340 - 25y
  x = (340 - 25y) / 20
  Since x has to be a whole number, we can try different values of y to see which one gives us a whole number for x.
  If y = 0, then x = 17, which is a whole number.
  If y = 1, then x = 15.75, which is not a whole number.
  If y = 2, then x = 14.5, which is not a whole number.
  If y = 3, then x = 13.25, which is not a whole number.
  If y = 4, then x = 12, which is a whole number.
  Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins that the coin-diver brought is 12.
  The answer is D: 1.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 72 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number.
Choices:
  A: 368
  B: 377
  C: 288
  D: 997
  E: 112
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let the three digit number be represented by abc, where a, b, and c are digits.
  We know that a + b + c = 17 and a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109.
  We also know that 100a + 10b + c - 495 = 100c + 10b + a.
  Simplifying the equation above, we get 99a - 99c = 495, which gives a - c = 5.
  We can use the two equations a + b + c = 17 and a - c = 5 to solve for a, b, and c.
  Solving for a, we get a = (22 + 5)/2 = 13/2, which is not a digit. Therefore, we made an error in our calculations.
  Let's try the answer choices:
  - If we try A: 368, we get a + b + c = 17 and a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 149, which does not satisfy the second equation. Therefore, A is not the answer.
  - If we try B: 377, we get a + b + c = 17 and a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 123, which does not satisfy the second equation. Therefore, B is not the answer.
  - If we try C: 288, we get a + b + c = 18 and a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 104, which satisfies both equations. Therefore, C is a possible answer.
  - If we try D: 997, we get a + b + c = 25 and a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 243, which does not satisfy the first equation. Therefore, D is not the answer.
  - If we try E: 112, we get a + b + c = 4 and a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 6, which does not satisfy the first equation. Therefore, E is not the answer.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 288.

Question: The ratio of the volumes of a cube to that of the sphere which will fit inside the cube is?
Choices:
  A: 2: π
  B: 7:2
  C: 8:2
  D: 6: π
  E: 8:3

  The diameter of the sphere will be equal to the side of the cube.
  The volume of the cube is a^3.
  The volume of the sphere is (4/3)πr^3, where r = a/2.
  The ratio of the volumes of the cube to the sphere is a^3 : (4/3)π(a/2)^3.
  Simplifying this expression, we get 6 : π.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 6: π.

  B: 105
  C: 126
  D: 252
  E: 525

  The second group can be formed in 5C5 ways (since we are selecting all 5 remaining bottles).
  Therefore, the total number of ways to create these 2 groups is 10C5 * 5C5 = 252.
  The answer is D: 252.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 76 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: All 250 files on Sam's hard drive are infected by either a virus or a worm or both. The number of files that are infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files that are infected by both a virus and a worm. If 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, how many of Sam's files were NOT infected by a worm?
Choices:
  A: 50
  B: 70
  C: 75
  D: 100
  E: 125
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's use a Venn diagram to represent the information given in the problem.
  Let V be the set of files infected by a virus, and W be the set of files infected by a worm.
  We know that V ∪ W = 250 (all files are either infected by a virus or a worm or both).
  Let x be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  We know that the number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5x.
  We can use this information to fill in the Venn diagram.
  We also know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, which means that the number of files infected by a virus is 125.
  We can use this information to find x and the number of files not infected by a worm.

Action: Answer("75")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's use a Venn diagram to solve the problem.
  Let x be the number of files infected only by a virus.
  Let y be the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm.
  Let z be the number of files infected only by a worm.
  We know that x + y + z = 250.
  We also know that z = 2.5y.
  We know that 50% of the files were not infected by a virus, so x + y = 125.
  We can use substitution to solve for y.
  x + y + z = 250
  x + y + 2.5y = 250
  x + 3.5y = 250
  x + y = 125
  x = 125 - y
  (125 - y) + 3.5y = 250
  2.5y = 125
  y = 50
  So, z = 2.5y = 125
  And x = 125 - y = 75
  The number of files not infected by a worm is x = 75.

  From the problem, we know that:
  - V + W + X = 250 (since all 250 files are infected by either a virus or a worm or both)
  - W = 2.5X (since the number of files infected only by a worm is 2.5 times the number of files infected by both a virus and a worm)
  - V = 0.5(250) = 125 (since 50% of the files were not infected by a virus)
  We want to find the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm, which is equal to V (since V represents the number of files infected only by a virus).
  We can solve for X using the second equation, substitute X into the first equation, and solve for V.

Response 3:
Thought:
  Let's use a Venn diagram to represent the information given in the problem.
  Let's use the following variables:
    - w: number of files infected only by a worm
    - v: number of files infected only by a virus
    - b: number of files infected by both a virus and a worm
  We know that:
    - w = 2.5b
    - v + w + b = 250
    - v = 0.5(250) = 125
  We can use the second equation to solve for b:
    - v + w + b = 250
    - 125 + w + b = 250
    - w + b = 125
    - b = 125 - w
  Substituting b in terms of w in the first equation:
    - w = 2.5(125 - w)
    - w = 312.5 - 2.5w
    - 3.5w = 312.5
    - w = 89
  Therefore, there are 89 files infected only by a worm.
  We want to find the number of files that were NOT infected by a worm:
    - Number of files NOT infected by a worm = Number of total files - Number of files infected by a worm
    - Number of files NOT infected by a worm = 250 - 89
    - Number of files NOT infected by a worm = 161
  The answer is E: 161.

  W + X = 125
  W = 2.5X
  Substituting W = 2.5X into the second equation, we get:
  2.5X + X = 125
  3.5X = 125
  X = 35.71 (rounded to two decimal places)
  W = 2.5X = 89.29 (rounded to two decimal places)
  The number of files that were not infected by a worm is V + X = 125 + 35.71 = 160.71 (rounded to two decimal places).
  Therefore, the answer is closest to D: 100.

Question: A trader sold an article at a profit of 20% for Rs.360. What is the cost price of the article?
Choices:
  A: 270
  B: 300
  C: 280
  D: 320
  E: 315
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the cost price of the article is x.
  The trader sold the article at a profit of 20%, which means the selling price is 1.2x.
  We know that the selling price is Rs.360.
  Therefore, 1.2x = 360.
  Solving for x, we get x = 300.
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let CP be the cost price of the article.
  Profit% = 20%
  Selling Price = Rs.360
  We know that Selling Price = Cost Price + Profit
  Therefore, 360 = CP + 20% of CP
  360 = CP + 0.2CP
  360 = 1.2CP
  CP = 360/1.2
  CP = 300
  Therefore, the cost price of the article is Rs.300.

Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the hotel buys x newspapers on Monday.
  The hotel buys twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week, so it buys 2x newspapers on Sunday.
  The hotel buys x newspapers each day from Monday to Saturday.
  The hotel buys 2x + x + x + x + x + x + x = 7x + 2 newspapers per week.
  The hotel pays $4 for each Sunday newspaper and $1 for each newspaper from Monday to Saturday.
  The hotel pays 4(2x) + x + x + x + x + x + x = 9x + 4 dollars per week.
  We know that the hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers.
  Therefore, 9x + 4x = 210
  Solving for x, we get x = 15.
  Therefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.
  The answer is A: 15.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's call the number of newspapers bought on Monday "x".
  The number of newspapers bought on Sunday is twice the number bought on Monday, so it is "2x".
  The number of newspapers bought on the other days of the week is the same every day, so it is "(1/5)(210 - 4 - 6x)".
  We subtract 4 from 210 because 4 newspapers are bought on Sunday, and we subtract 6x because 1 newspaper is bought on Monday and 2 newspapers are bought on Sunday for every 3 newspapers bought the rest of the days of the week.
  The total cost of the newspapers is $210, so we can set up the equation: 4(2x) + 1(x) + 5(1/5)(210 - 4 - 6x) = 210.
  Simplifying the equation, we get: 8x + x + 210 - 4 - 6x = 210, which becomes 3x = 4.
  Therefore, x = 4/3.
  However, we need to round up to the nearest whole number because we cannot buy a fraction of a newspaper.
  The only answer choice that is greater than 4/3 and a multiple of 5 is 15.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
- Let's assume that the hotel buys x newspapers on Monday.
- On Sunday, the hotel buys twice as many newspapers as it does on Monday, so it buys 2x newspapers.
- The hotel buys 7 newspapers in a week, so it buys (7-1)*x + 2x = 6x + 4 newspapers.
- The hotel pays $210 per week for newspapers, so 6x + 4 newspapers cost $210.
- We can solve for x to find how many newspapers the hotel buys on Monday.
- 6x + 4 = 210
- 6x = 206
- x = 34.33
- The hotel cannot buy a fraction of a newspaper, so it must buy either 34 or 35 newspapers on Monday.
- If the hotel buys 34 newspapers on Monday, it buys 2*34 = 68 newspapers on Sunday, and 68+34 = 102 newspapers in total.
- The cost of 102 newspapers is (1*6 + 4)*34 = $714.
- This is more than $210, so the hotel must buy fewer newspapers on Monday.
- If the hotel buys 35 newspapers on Monday, it buys 2*35 = 70 newspapers on Sunday, and 70+35 = 105 newspapers in total.
- The cost of 105 newspapers is (1*6 + 4)*35 = $735.
- This is more than $210, so the hotel must buy even fewer newspapers on Monday.
- The only option left is 30 newspapers on Monday.
- The hotel buys 2*30 = 60 newspapers on Sunday, and 60+30 = 90 newspapers in total.
- The cost of 90 newspapers is (1*6 + 4)*30 = $210.
- This is the correct answer.

  We can find the new length by multiplying the original length by (3/5).

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume that the distance between X and Y is d km.
  Let's assume that they meet for the second time after t hours.
  In the first t/2 hours, Allen covers (54 * t/2) km = 27t km.
  In the first t/2 hours, Bob covers (78 * t/2) km = 39t km.
  In the second t/2 hours, Allen covers (54 * t/2) km = 27t km.
  In the second t/2 hours, Bob covers (78 * t/2) km = 39t km.
  The total distance covered by Allen in both directions is 2 * 27t = 54t km.
  The total distance covered by Bob in both directions is 2 * 39t = 78t km.
  We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  Therefore, 78t - 54t = 48
  Solving for t, we get t = 4 hours.
  The distance between X and Y is d = 2 * 27t = 216 km.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 144km.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let the distance between X and Y be d.
  Let the time taken by Allen to reach Y be t.
  Let the time taken by Bob to reach X be t1.
  Since they meet twice, the total time taken by Allen to travel from X to Y and back to X is 2t.
  The distance traveled by Allen from X to Y and back to X is 2d.
  The distance traveled by Bob from Y to X and back to Y is 2d.
  The distance traveled by Bob when they meet for the second time is d+48km.
  We can use the formula distance = speed x time to form equations.
  From the given information, we can form the following equations:
    d = 54t + 78t1
    2d = 54t + 78t1 + 54t
    2d = 78t1 + 108t
    d + 48 = 78t1
    Substituting the value of d from the third equation in the fourth equation, we get:
    2d - 48 = 78t1
    2d = 78t1 + 48
    Substituting the value of 2d from the third equation in the fifth equation, we get:
    78t1 + 108t - 48 = 78t1
    108t = 48
    t = 2/9 hours
    Substituting the value of t in the first equation, we get:
    d = 54 x 2/9 + 78t1
    d = 12 + 78t1
    Substituting the value of t in the second equation, we get:
    2d = 54 x 2/9 + 78t1 + 54 x 2/9
    2d = 24 + 78t1
    Subtracting the second equation from the third equation, we get:
    d = 84 km
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 84 km.
  The answer is D: 84 km.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let the distance between X and Y be d.
  Let the time taken for Allen to reach Y be t.
  Let the time taken for Bob to reach X be t1.
  Distance covered by Allen = d/2
  Distance covered by Bob = 78t
  Distance covered by Allen in the return journey = d/2
  Distance covered by Bob in the return journey = 78(t1-t)
  We know that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen.
  Therefore, 78t - d/2 = d/2 + 78(t1-t) + 48
  Simplifying the above equation, we get t1 = 2t + 2
  Distance between X and Y = Distance covered by Allen + Distance covered by Bob
  Distance between X and Y = d/2 + d/2 + 78(t1-t)
  Distance between X and Y = d + 78(2t + 2 - t)
  Distance between X and Y = d + 78(t + 2)
  We know that distance covered by Bob = 78t
  Therefore, d + 78(t + 2) - 78t = 48
  Simplifying the above equation, we get d = 144 km
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 144 km.

Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the distance travelled by the jeep is "d" km.
  Let's assume the speed of the jeep in the forward journey is "s" km/hr.
  Then, the speed of the jeep in the return journey is "s+12" km/hr.
  We know that distance = speed x time.
  In the forward journey, the jeep took 6 hours to travel the distance "d" km at a speed of "s" km/hr.
  Therefore, d = 6s.
  In the return journey, the jeep took 4 hours to travel the same distance "d" km at a speed of "s+12" km/hr.
  Therefore, d = 4(s+12).
  Equating both the equations, we get 6s = 4(s+12).
  Solving this equation, we get s = 18.
  Therefore, d = 6s = 6 x 18 = 108 km.
  The answer is not present in the choices.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the number of lilies after n days is 2^(n/2).
  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies.
  Therefore, 2^(60/2) = 2^30 = the number of lilies on the lake after 60 days.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, then the number of lilies after n days is 64 * 2^(n/2).
  We want to find the number of days it takes for the lake to be fully covered with lilies, which means the number of lilies is equal to 2^30.
  Therefore, we need to solve the equation 64 * 2^(n/2) = 2^30 for n.
  Dividing both sides by 64, we get 2^(n/2) = 2^25.
  Taking the logarithm base 2 of both sides, we get n/2 = 25.
  Multiplying both sides by 2, we get n = 50.
  Therefore, the lake will be fully covered with lilies after 50 days.
  The answer is not one of the available choices, but the closest one is D: 53.
Action: Answer("D")

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 84 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's call the weight of the new heavy duty truck "x".
  The total weight of the 10 vehicles before adding the new truck is 10 * 12.2 = 122 tons.
  The total weight of the 11 vehicles after adding the new truck is 11 * (12.2 + 2.6) = 157.2 tons.
  The total weight of the 10 original vehicles is 122 tons, so the weight of the new truck is the difference between the total weight of all 11 vehicles and the weight of the 10 original vehicles.
  The weight of the new truck is 157.2 - 122 = 35.2 tons.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 40.8.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's call the weight of the new heavy duty truck "x".
  The sum of the weights of the original 10 vehicles is 10 * 12.2 = 122.
  After adding the new truck, there are 11 vehicles in the group.
  The new average weight is 12.2 + 2.6 = 14.8.
  The sum of the weights of all 11 vehicles is 11 * 14.8 = 162.8.
  The sum of the weights of the original 10 vehicles plus the weight of the new truck is 122 + x.
  We can set up an equation: (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  Solving for x: 122 + x = 162.8
  x = 40.8
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 40.8 tons.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Thought:
- The current mixture is 30% sand and 70% clay.
- We want to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.
- This means we want the mixture to be 50% sand and 50% clay.
- We need to remove some of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
- Let's assume we remove x kg of the mixture.
- The amount of sand in the remaining mixture is 0.3(10 - x) kg.
- We want to add x kg of pure sand to the mixture.
- The total amount of sand in the new mixture is 0.3(10 - x) + x kg.
- We want this to be equal to 50% of the new mixture, which is (10 - x + x) / 2 = 5 kg.
- Setting up the equation: 0.3(10 - x) + x = 5
- Solving for x: 3 - 0.3x + x = 5, 0.7x = 2, x = 20/7
- Therefore, we need to remove 20/7 kg of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
Action: Answer("B")

  B = 170-L

  Cost of gardening the boundary = Area of the boundary * 10

  Area of the rectangular plot = L*(170-L)
  Area of the rectangular plot with the boundary = (L+2x)(170-L+2x)
  Area of the boundary = (L+2x)(170-L+2x) - L*(170-L)

  2(L+B) = 340
  L+B = 170
  B = 170-L

  Area of the rectangular plot = L*(170-L)
  Area of the rectangular plot with the boundary = (L+2x)(170-L+2x)
  Area of the boundary = (L+2x)(170-L+2x) - L*(170-L)
  Cost of gardening the boundary = (L+2x)(170-L+2x - L)*(10)

  Area of the boundary = (L+2x)(170-L+2x) - L*(170-L)
  Area of the boundary = 170L - L^2 + 4xL + 340x - 2x^2 - 170L + L^2
  Area of the boundary = 4xL - 2x^2 + 340x

  Cost of gardening the boundary = (L+2x)(170-L+2x - L)*(10)
  Cost of gardening the boundary = (L+2x)(170-2L+2x)*(10)
  Cost of gardening the boundary = (L*10 + 20x)*(170-2L+2x)
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 10L(170-2L+2x) + 20x(170-2L+2x)
  Cost of gardening the boundary = 20Lx - 2L^2 + 340x - 4xL + 340x - 40x^2
  Cost of gardening the boundary = -2L^2 + 20Lx - 40x^2 + 680x

  20L - 80x + 680 = 0
  20L + 680 = 80x
  x = (20L + 680)/80

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cost price of 1 kg of oranges is 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The selling price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50.
  The profit made on 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50.
  The profit made on 90 kg of oranges is 90 x Rs. 2.50 = Rs. 225.
  The percentage gain is (profit/cost price) x 100.
  The percentage gain is (225/450) x 100 = 50%.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 50%.

  B: 26 days
  C: 27 days
  D: 28 days
  E: 29 days

  However, the frog will come out on the 30th day, so it will have jumped up 3m but not fallen back 2m.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume Joe's age is J, Joe's sister's age is S, and Joe's father's age is F.
  We know that J + S + F = 100.
  We also know that when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now.
  Let's assume x is the number of years until Joe is as old as his father.
  Then, J + x = F + x
  S + x = 2S
  Therefore, S = x
  We also know that when Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father.
  Let's assume y is the number of years until Joe is as old as his father.
  Then, F + y = 2(S + y)
  We can simplify this equation to F + y = 2S + 2y
  We know that S = x, so we can substitute S with x.
  F + y = 2x + 2y
  We also know that J + S + F = 100, so we can substitute S with 100 - J - F.
  J + (100 - J - F) + F = 100
  Simplifying this equation, we get F = 50.
  Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 50.
  The answer is C: 50.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume Joe's age is J, his sister's age is S and his father's age is F.
  We know that J + S + F = 100.
  We also know that when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now.
  Let's assume that when Joe is as old as his father, they will both be x years old.
  So, we have two equations:
  x = J + F
  2S = S + x
  Solving the above equations, we get:
  S = x/2
  J = x - F
  Substituting these values in the first equation, we get:
  x - F + x/2 + F = 100
  Solving for F, we get:
  F = 50
  Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 50.
  The answer is C: 50.

  We can then substitute S into J + S + F = 100 and solve for F.
  The answer is F = 55.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Thought:
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan for each head.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher for each tail.
  Let's assume that the coin landed on heads x times.
  Therefore, the coin landed on tails (20-x) times.
  Christopher gave $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan gave $3 to Christopher (20-x) times.
  The total amount of money exchanged is 2x + 3(20-x) = 60 - x.
  Since the total amount of money exchanged is zero, we have 60 - x = 0.
  Solving for x, we get x = 60.
  Therefore, the coin landed on heads 10 times.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan each time the coin lands on Heads.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher each time the coin lands on Tails.

  Christopher gave $2 to Jonathan x times.
  Jonathan gave $3 to Christopher y times.
  Christopher neither won nor lost any amount, so he gave $2x and received $3y.
  Therefore, 2x = 3y.
  The total number of flips is 20, so x + y = 20.
  We can solve the system of equations to find x and y.
  Multiplying the first equation by 2, we get 4x = 6y.
  Dividing by 2, we get 2x = 3y.
  Substituting into the second equation, we get 2x + x = 20.
  Simplifying, we get 3x = 20.
  Therefore, x = 6.666... which is not a whole number.
  This means that the coin did not land on Heads a whole number of times.
  However, we know that the coin did not land on Heads or Tails a total of 20 times.
  Therefore, the coin must have landed on Heads 10 times and Tails 10 times.
  The answer is A: 10.

Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's call the distance between A and B "d".
  Let's call the time it takes Kevin to travel from A to B "t".
  We know that Kevin drove at a constant speed of 70 mph from A to B, so we can use the formula distance = rate x time to get d = 70t.
  We also know that Kevin turned around and drove back to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Let's call the time it takes him to travel from B to A "t2". We can use the formula distance = rate x time to get d = 90t2.
  We know that Kevin was 70 miles away from B exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip. Let's call the total time of his trip "T". We can use the formula T = t + t2 to get t2 = T - t - 3.
  We can now substitute t2 into the equation d = 90t2 to get d = 90(T - t - 3).
  We can substitute d = 70t into this equation to get 70t = 90(T - t - 3).
  We can simplify this equation to get 7t = 9(T - t - 3).
  We can simplify further to get 7t = 9T - 9t - 27.
  We can solve for t to get t = (9/16)T - (27/16).
  We can substitute this value of t into the equation d = 70t to get d = (63/8)T - (189/8).
  We can now solve for T using the fact that Kevin was 70 miles away from B exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip. We know that he was driving at 90 mph at that point, so he had (70/90) hours = (7/9) hours left to travel. We can use this to get T = t + t2 + (7/9) = 2t + (7/9).
  We can substitute this value of T into the equation for d to get d = (63/8)(2t + (7/9)) - (189/8) = (567t + 126)/8.
  We can now substitute the value of t we found earlier to get d = (567/8)((9/16)T - (27/16)) + (126/8) = (567/128)T + (135/8).
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is (567/128)T + (135/8).
  To find the answer, we need to select the choice that gives us a distance in this form.
  Choice A: 180 = (567/128)T + (135/8) is not true for any value of T.
  Choice B: 90 = (567/128)T + (135/8) is not true for any value of T.
  Choice C: 270 = (567/128)T + (135/8) is not true for any value of T.
  Choice D: 360 = (567/128)T + (135/8) is true for T = 192.
  Therefore, the answer is D: 360.

Question: I know a 5 digit number having a property that with a 1 after it, it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it.
What is that number?
Choices:
  A: 42857
  B: 32456
  C: 76523
  D: 24567
  E: 43566

  If we add 1 before the number, it becomes 1abcde.
  We know that abcde1 is three times as large as 1abcde.
  So, we can write an equation as follows:
  3(100000a + 10000b + 1000c + 100d + 10e + 1) = 100000 + 10000a + 1000b + 100c + 10d + e
  Simplifying the equation, we get:
  299999a + 29999b + 2999c + 299d + 29e = 99999
  Since the left-hand side of the equation is divisible by 29, the right-hand side must also be divisible by 29.
  The only 5-digit number that satisfies this condition is 42857.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 42857.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the number of employees in the organization is "x".
  Each employee contributed "y" amount of money.
  The total amount collected without the extra Rs. 60 is 6 lakhs.
  Therefore, xy = 6,00,000
  The total amount collected with the extra Rs. 60 is 6.24 lakhs.
  Therefore, x(y+60) = 6,24,000
  By solving these two equations, we can find the value of x.
  xy + 60x = 6,24,000
  6,00,000 + 60x = 6,24,000
  60x = 24,000
  x = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.
  The answer is C: 400.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's assume that there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  Each employee contributes 'x' amount of money.
  The total amount collected is Rs. 6 lakh.
  Therefore, 6 lakh = n * x
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the total contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh.
  This means that the total amount collected increased by Rs. 24,000 (6.24 lakh - 6 lakh).
  We know that each employee contributed Rs. 60 extra.
  Therefore, the number of employees is given by (24000/60) + n = 400 + n.
  We can solve for n by equating the two expressions for the number of employees.
  6 lakh / x = 400 + n
  x = 1500
  n = 6 lakh / x = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Let's assume there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  Each employee contributed 'x' amount of money.
  Therefore, the total amount contributed by 'n' employees is n*x.
  According to the problem, n*x = 6,00,000.
  If each employee had contributed Rs. 60 extra, then the total contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh.
  So, n*(x+60) = 6,24,000.
  By solving these two equations, we can find the value of 'n'.
  n = (6,24,000 - 6,00,000) / 60
  n = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in that organization.
  The answer is C: 400.

### Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Thought:
Let's assume the amount each nephew receives is "x".
Each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, so each daughter receives 4x.
Each son receives five times as much as each nephew, so each son receives 5x.
The total number of people who receive the money is 5+4+2=11.
The total amount of money is Rs 8600.
We can set up the equation: 5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600
Simplifying the equation: 25x + 16x + 2x = 8600/11
Solving for x: 43x = 780
x = 18
Each daughter receives 4x = 4(18) = 72.
Therefore, each daughter receives Rs 72.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let the amount received by each nephew be x.
Amount received by each daughter = 4x
Amount received by each son = 5x
Total number of children = 5 sons + 4 daughters + 2 nephews = 11
Total amount = Rs 8600
Therefore, (5*5x) + (4*4x) + (2*x) = 8600
Simplifying the above equation, we get x = 200
Amount received by each daughter = 4x = 4*200 = Rs 800
Therefore, the answer is E: Rs 800.

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the number is "x".
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number, which is (7/18)*x.
  The actual value of 7/8 of the number is (7/8)*x.
  The difference between the student's answer and the actual answer is 770.
  Therefore, (7/8)*x - (7/18)*x = 770.
  Simplifying the equation, we get (35/72)*x = 770.

Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles

  Therefore, the cab can travel 500 / 10 = 50 additional quarter-miles.
  The total distance that can be traveled is 1 + 50/4 = 13 miles.
  Therefore, the maximum distance that can be traveled is 13 miles.
